A Laughing Matter 108

— Sea Traveler

Judge: This is a courtroom, a very solemn place. Anyone who dares to make noise, cause trouble, and disobey order will be expelled!

A Criminal (gesticulating wildly and laughing loudly): Hahahaha! This bird courtroom... what's so rare and worthy of making such a fuss about?

Judge: Hey, criminal, what does this mean?

A Criminal: I'm making noise and causing trouble! Why don't you expel me?

Mother: Good child, why are you crying? Who bullied you?

Young Daughter: Mommy, Brother broke my foreign doll!

Mother: You naughty child, how did he break your foreign doll?

Young Daughter: I hit his head with the foreign doll, and his head broke my foreign doll.

Father (to his grown daughter): Since you two love each other, and love has led to talk of marriage, this is a very proper step, and your father has no reason to object. However, I want to ask, what kind of person is he? Can he handle you?

Daughter: He's very strong. When I sit on him, he never complains.

Man: Miss B, do you like puppies?

Woman: I've always liked them very much, but see how I treat you.

The Filial Piety of Master Zeng Nongran 109

— Zhang Shanzi

My teacher, Master Zeng of Hengyang, has been renowned for his writing since his youth, and in recent twenty years for his calligraphy, and in his old age especially for his painting. Everyone who knows the master admires his writing, calligraphy, and painting. However, what the master has that is praiseworthy and exemplary lies outside of his writing, calligraphy, and painting. Therefore, Mr. Zu'an praised the master's portrait, saying: "His conduct can subdue an era, and his virtue nurtures himself. His learning is sufficient to pursue the three ancient times, and his transformation is not limited to people. Calligraphy and painting are merely his extracurricular activities." Mr. Zu'an treated Hengyang like an elder brother for thirty years and knew him most truly. Among the disciples, Shanzi and his younger brother Daqian were closest to the master, visiting frequently. After discussing painting, they would continue into the night. Every time they spoke, he would earnestly advise them on filial piety. Once, when mentioning the Boxer Rebellion in the year of Gengzi, he carried his mother, the Grand Matriarch, out of the capital wearing short clothes and walked thousands of miles. Upon arriving in Hangzhou, he was filled with excitement and then burst into tears. His innate filial piety can be seen in general. In the year of Guihai, Shanzi and his younger brother Daqian welcomed and supported him and were deeply appreciated, and he bestowed upon them a long couplet: "Madam Guan's family is rich in painting, white hair waving a brush, colorful clothes holding an inkstone; Grand Commandant Pan's ten thousand cups of silk and bamboo, palanquin warm in the sun, orchids in the breeze." Now that Mount Tai is about to collapse, stroking his beard and chasing after his beard, his spirit is uniquely mournful. Recalling his 67th birthday, he wrote a snow scene and inscribed a poem: "I have lived sixty-seven years, three months in one year become an orphan. Mother's weeping, children's laughter, I do not know the hardship of raising. Fifty-five years I have lived, at fourteen mother abandoned me, I did not expect to live to this day. Every year the family celebrates with wine, I alone secretly weep, looking up to heaven. In those years, the broken house where mother lived, father sick for years relying on mother's strength. Born in the ice and snow, drinking cold water as breakfast. The neighbor quickly brought ginger soup, swept away the snow to wash the child, a long sigh. I dare not recall the bitterness of my life, teaching scriptures under the knees, weaving under the moon. Unable to repay the kindness, I only pierce my heart, this life, this pain, how can it end? Clouds deep under South Mountain, only dreams connect morning and evening. Planning to enter South Mountain with a writing brush, in old age relying on mother's grave to cut thorns." He also sent a painting album to his second brother, Jiyin, with a postscript: "This album was made in the winter of Yichou, and there are also untiled frames. Now, suddenly four years have passed again. It is mounted and sent with a supplemental title to Shu Nan, who is forty years old this year. I still remember that when I was forty, it was the year of Gengzi. I carried my mother and took you flying from the Grand Canal to the south to escape the Boxer Rebellion. You were twelve years old, your brother was fourteen years old, and your younger brother was eight years old. Your mother died in Beijing in her early years, and the late Queen Mother, at sixty-nine, wept with you morning and evening. I, wearing short clothes with only one servant, went through a hundred hardships. Now it is still vivid as yesterday, and I did not realize I was sixty-eight and you were forty years old. I went out and immediately ordered you to live in Heng to guard the tombs of the ancestors and mothers. In this world, it is fortunate to seek not to starve. Be diligent and hard-working, keep your body loyal and your ambitions honest. Seek to be one step lower than others in everything, so you will have extra place for yourself." Shu Nan respectfully notes this in the twenty-second day of the fifth month of Wuchen, recording this as a training for tending the courtyard. A poem and a postscript, repeatedly savored, are merely a record of filial piety. From this, we can see that our master's filial piety, although innate, also stems from the Queen Mother's fostering of the orphaned heart. Now there are sons and grandsons, and grandsons have sons again. My generation of elder brothers are all talented in correcting the family. Those who come out late, such as the one who is a barrier, are also outstanding and intelligent. The family's reputation is not easy, and it is always necessary to take the master's heart as the heart (repay).

Recording the Coffin of Former President Tan 110

— Lanxi

President Tan of the Executive Yuan, a member of the National Government, has passed away. This is truly a deeply shocking event. The National Government has instructed the Ministry of Finance to allocate 10,000 yuan for funeral expenses, which shows the respect for the virtuous and the courtesy. At around 10:20 a.m. on September 23, a coffin was transported to the North Station by a certain funeral shop. The coffin was much larger than ordinary ones. It was unpainted, with a yellow and bright color, and was made of nanmu wood. Many people at the station crowded around to view it. When the coffin was lifted off the freight car and onto the station ground, we stroked the wood with our hands for a while. The material was excellent, smooth, and lovely, worth 3,000 taels of silver. After the coffin lid was opened, there were still several pieces of black carved nanmu boards, which were quite exquisite. Six or seven men carried the coffin, each with their eyes wide open and their teeth bared, indicating that they had exerted a lot of effort. The coffin was lifted onto the car and will be transported to Nanjing, where painting work will begin.

Recording the Radio Scientist of Zhongxing 111

— Laborer

Not feeling easy living in Shanghai and suffering from long-term poverty, I was considering moving elsewhere. After being persuaded by my friends, I traveled to Ningbo and met Pan Ziye, a member of the Bank of China here. Observing his behavior, I felt even more respect for him. Therefore, I express this.

Pan Zi, named Yelu, is a native of Kunshan, Jiangsu. When he first arrived in Ningbo, he often relieved his loneliness by browsing books and newspapers. Because he was not good at foreign languages, he often suffered from not being able to read texts from other countries. When the Northern Expeditionary Army rose up and the southeast was settled, local labor unrest also arose. Pan initiated and organized a club and established a radio station to spread commercial information. His colleagues also enjoyed the pleasure of listening to it. It was truly a fast way to do two things at once. His colleagues hired Pan to be the manager. Since then, Pan has been immersed in research, often staying up past midnight, and his interest is strong. When the mechanical structure became clear, he then worked hard to specialize in Western languages, so that he could buy and read foreign works to learn from others. Soon, he was able to manufacture various broadcasting machines. Mr. Su Zugui, the director of the radio department of the Shanghai Asian American Company, was introduced to Mr. Pan by a friend and was surprised to find that he was a genius. Pan's skills were purely derived from his heart, which was not an easy thing. When Pan went to Shanghai on business, he would definitely go to Mr. Su's place to ask for advice, so that his learning became more and more refined. He is now recognized by the people of the county as a radio expert in Ningbo City. I saw Pan working on designs at his desk after work, and they were exquisitely beautiful. Someone who has not been well-educated could not possibly have achieved this. It is truly a strange thing.

All Quiet on the Western Front 112

— Ye Xinfo

After the end of the European War, Western material civilization suddenly went bankrupt, and human thought was deeply stimulated. As a result, Lao-Zhuang's learning in our country became quite popular in their land. The film, novel, and drama industries produced a large number of anti-war works. In terms of film, "Flowers in the Battlefield" and "Nightingale in the Battlefield" were the most famous, but they were mostly love romantic or legendary styles. Now, only "All Quiet on the Western Front" is unique, penetrating into the marrow and brain of mankind, and will never be forgotten. It completely depicts the cruelty and inhumanity of war and killing, showing the war situation nakedly to the reader, and there is much to be said about its good intentions.

A person cries bitterly as soon as they enter the world, and sobs when they die. Love and gold are taken away, and they suffer from diseases and beasts. On a grander scale, there is the conflict between nations and the strong preying on the weak. Natural selection is a common law. The killings in history have become an inevitable step. How much glory and happiness can mankind obtain? The desire for goods does not stop, and the killing of mankind has no limit. This is why Buddhism advocates passivity. There is a reason why humanity is increased. In addition to implying the origin of Buddhist thought, "All Quiet on the Western Front" also depicts the foolishness and hegemony of military nationalists and current governments that advocate only loving their own nations and cruelly harming mankind. It reveals everywhere that the so-called 20th-century civilization has not yet solved the biggest problem of mankind. The world's great scientists work tirelessly for years, and the result is the creation of a weapon for a part of them to kill their own kind. Scientists watching this film are enough to stamp their feet and regret their deaths. Great politicians, great scholars, and great thinkers watching this film will not lose their voices and sink into contemplation, citing it as a human shame. When the world's conventions are exhausted and seven things are seen, the release of this film is more beneficial than holding several international gatherings. The whole film depicts the scenes of artillery fire and rain. When they charged, counterattacked, fought hand-to-hand, and drank bullets to death, it was heartbreaking, and it made people suspect that mankind would never have such a cruel and violent act. In the film, there is a Paul, who was encouraged by a cruel teacher in his student days and joined the army with his classmates, and he personally killed the enemy. Later, he obtained a family photo of the enemy from his bag and looked at it for a long time, with tears in his voice. The audience was moved to tears. When he took leave to return home, he was saddened by the sight and could not restrain himself, almost regarding his mother and sister as people from another world, and his house as ruins. It is heart-wrenching to watch!

Travel Notes in Southeast Asia (60) 113

— Linghua

The Reporters of Southeast Asia — Liu

Smart reporters probably don't talk much, avoiding political criticism to avoid trouble. If they have to say something, it's about romance, coolness, and antiques. It's difficult to be a reporter in Southeast Asia because it's easy to talk to rational people, but difficult to talk to emotional friends. The culturally backward people of Southeast Asia are already amazing for knowing how to read newspapers. How is it possible to expect them to analyze facts rationally? — Therefore, every reporter, intellectual, and worker determines his will by his life, not by determining his life by his will. So, the newspapers of Southeast Asia generally carry a brownish-gray color and can be regarded as a social photograph.

However, reporters in Southeast Asia also have things that are easier than in the country: (1) They don't pay much attention to writing. As long as they can barely write a few hundred words, it counts as an article. Whether the content is logical or meaningful is not important. So, people who like to read without seeking thorough understanding and people who don't like to read but like to seek thorough understanding can both be reporters in Southeast Asia. (2) There is considerable legal protection. If you offend an important person in the country, you will immediately be beheaded or imprisoned. In Southeast Asia, you will at most be deported. However, your livelihood will be lost, and your life is in the same danger. However, it also depends on whether the [ghost] soul is stronger than the body that dies first.

Mr. Liu described the situation of reporters in Southeast Asia like this. According to the Commemorative Publication in Singapore, the Singapore Daily is the most advanced newspaper in Southeast Asia. His self-description may have some modesty and encouragement, but from this, one can get a glimpse of the situation of the Southeast Asian newspaper industry. In Singapore, newspapers do not come out in the morning. All newspapers come out at 4:00 PM in the afternoon. The newspapers in Annam are also like this, but there are morning newspapers in Penang, which is different. Government inspections are mostly in the afternoon and must be checked before they are allowed to be published. However, it is heard that the laws of the Dutch territories are different from those of the British territories. In the Dutch territories, the government does not inspect in advance and can be freely published. However, if something illegal is found after publication, it will be punished.

Eastern Travels Correspondence (20) 114

— Wu Xiaohou

(3) Asakusa Park

Asakusa Park is located in the Asakusa district. Most of the land for Asakusa Park was formerly the site of Sensō-ji Temple. In the sixth year of the Meiji era (1873), it was incorporated as a park by decree of the Dajō-kan (Grand Council of State). Since the Edo period, it has been a famous place for common people to visit. Formerly, the central area was the Kannondō Hall, with the North Valley to the north and the East Valley to the east. The Nakamise shopping street to the south was also called South Valley. Therefore, the park can be divided into seven areas: The first area is the vicinity of the Kannondō Hall; the second area is the area in front of the Niōmon Gate and the Nakamise shopping street; the third area is the Denbō-in Temple; the fourth area is the planting area west of the Kannondō Hall and the area near the gourd-shaped pond; the fifth area is north of the Kannondō Hall; the sixth area is the area west and south of the large pond; and the seventh area is the first and second blocks on both sides of the Nakamise shopping street and the third block southwest of Benten-yama and the street. What is called the Kaminarimon Gate now only exists in name and the dilapidated foundation stones. In front of the Nakamise shopping street is a stone path leading directly to the Niōmon Gate. In front is the Kannondō Hall, surrounded by extremely beautiful large ginkgo trees. Re-entering the Niōmon Gate, to the right is the five-story pagoda and the scripture hall, which houses the original edition of the Great Treasury Sutra, cherished as a national treasure. To the south of the pagoda is a small hill, Benten-yama, with a bell and drum tower built on it. On the bell are miscellaneous poems about Asakusa and Ueno. Below the hill is a pond and a children's playground. To the east of the Kannondō Hall is a gate called Nitenmon Gate, and to the north of it is the Sansha Shrine, with Kannon and Asakusa Shrine located there. To the west of the Kannondō Hall is the Awashima-dō pond. Since the Kamakura period, the stone lanterns of the six Jizō bodhisattvas have been passed down, and incense smoke has never ceased to this day. Behind the Kannondō Hall is a large open space with a large dragon god fountain, and the remaining water flows into the Awashima pond, then flows west through the planted area into the gourd-shaped pond. The stream is called the Ninety-Nine River. To the west of Awashima-dō are planted cherry, plum, and maple trees, and there are many old trees that have been there for many years. From here, planted with flowers and trees, a path for strolling leads directly into the woods near the gourd-shaped pond. The landscape is excellent, with highs and lows of the terrain, stone arrangements, forests, and springs. The ponds in the sixth district are all buried and marked in the rice fields. In the pond, there is a island called Omoteshū, and a figure-eight bridge makes it easy to cross. To the west and south of the large pond are designated areas for selling goods, as well as movie theaters and other halls, restaurants, etc., arranged in a row. The road is paved with stones, which is a new look compared to the past, and it is truly a place of joy for the people of the city. To the southwest of the Kannondō Temple is the garden of Denbō-in Temple, said to be the work of Kobori Enshū, with a natural style. National treasure forests and springs, and other halls and various scenic spots in the park, many restaurants, game fields, and entertainment businesses, but the garden area is only about 20,000 tsubo. The famous Fujiwara Hokō has written a poem as follows: The traces of the past are recorded as prosperity, and once passed life in the sea of vows. Also, as a poet, he appears in a white robe as an immortal, with white cherry blossoms.

(4) Inokashira Park

Inokashira Park is located between Musashino Village and Mitaka Village in Kita-Tama County, Tokyo Prefecture. It used to be an imperial forest. In the third year of the Taisho era (1914), it was donated to Tokyo City as a park. It was opened in May of the sixth year of the Taisho era (1917), about five chō south of Kichijōji Station on the Chūō Line. The terrain can be divided into two parts. West of the main gate is a plateau, belonging to Musashino Village, called Goten, with forests of cypress, oak, and thorns. To the west is the Tokyo Municipal Nursery Institute, the Juvenile Reformatory, and the Inokashira School, etc. To the southwest is Koganei Tamagawa, etc. To the east of the main gate is a low-lying area, commonly known as Yato, and below it is the Y-shaped Inokashira Pond, belonging to Mitaka Village. The pond is the source of the old Kanda River, and the water is clear and gurgling. The clear and transparent water allows you to see the fish and beautiful aquatic plants at the bottom, and the aquatic birds, fish, and plants are quite valuable for academic research. Next to the pond is the Benten Shrine, surrounded by a dense forest of tall old cedar trees, which is dark even during the day. Its shadow is often immersed in the water, which is also a magnificent sight. At the eastern end, near the water gate, there is a large open space. In the tenth year of the Taisho era (1921), this was used as a children's garden with a wading pond and a 60-meter swimming pool, which is very lively in the summer. There is an island in the pond with bridges on the left and right for easy crossing. There is a path along the pond for strolling, scattered with benches for visitors to sit and rest, and there are tea sellers. This can be called a natural forest park in the suburbs, a place for urbanites to relax. In spring there are flowers, in summer it's cool, and in autumn there are red leaves. On Sundays and holidays, there are various kinds of lively events.

Commercial News

Financial and Gold Markets Gradually Advancing 115

Yesterday, the 25th, the gold market continued its upward trend, showing swift and orderly progress, turning mediocrity into excellence. However, the total turnover for the one-two gold bar was only 6.5 taels throughout the day, showing a softening of sentiment. As for bills of exchange, they also tended to tighten, with the listed price already reduced by half a level. Trading in the market was quite active, with demand generally exceeding supply. Companies such as Yuan Maoyong, Yuan Chengyong, Han Heng, etc., were all buying, while Hengxing, Yixing, Shunli, etc., were all selling. In the morning, the situation was flat and soft, with a slight decrease in the silver market, which was not taken seriously. Later, buyers became active, and bills of exchange also rose frequently, soaring by four or five taels. However, there was a slight lull, and then the market broke out. Yongzhi, Fengyong, Yuan Xingyong, Yuan Chengyong, and Yong Fuchang all made purchases, while the Dalian group and others were still selling. At first, there was a slight softening, fearing that the silver market might rise, but then the buying enthusiasm increased, and bills of exchange became even more popular. The upward trend had already reached 49 taels, and the final price was between 48 taels.

Before the midday closing, the market went straight up. The opening price for November was slightly lower by 2 qian at 542.6 taels. The large gold bars and silver prices were only reduced by one-eighth. Because the European market was sluggish, sentiment was downward. Afterwards, buyers were diligent, and foreign exchange was also stable. Rice Market: Prosperity Reaches Its Peak and Declines 123

New Supplies Surge Daily, Sales Remain Quiet

Continuous Sharp Drops, New and Old Alike Dumped

In Zhabei, yesterday's inbound shipments from Luli Road were estimated at over forty, but market sales were sluggish. Buyers from all quarters, due to the rapid price decline, were generally inactive, while sellers were unusually eager to sell. Thus, new early rice saw another significant drop, with top-grade rice opening at sixteen yuan seventy-eight cents from a high of one yuan fifty cents, ordinary rice already around fifteen yuan, and medium-grade rice being heavily dumped at a price cut of about two yuan, opening at thirteen yuan seventy-eight cents. According to telegrams from Wuxi, the price of Wuxi early rice has returned to the eleven yuan mark, but there is still no good demand, so the Shanghai market is still difficult to stabilize. Although the arrival of Dongxin early rice is not significant, the downward trend is also sharp, falling by one yuan fifty cents to open at only fifteen yuan. Yangjian rice opened at a high of thirteen yuan, Dujian rice at thirteen yuan twenty cents, and lower grades down to twelve yuan or more, all down by about one yuan. Top-grade Kejian and Bujian rice are only between eleven yuan seventy-eight cents, with lower grades at ten yuan six cents, requiring a sharp price cut of one yuan to one yuan fifty cents. Such a decline is rare in recent years, with both early and late rice dropping by as much as five yuan this week.

In South Shanghai yesterday, over thirty boats arrived, and the entire street was watching. Due to the surge of new supplies and the subsequent sharp price drop of old broken rice, all remaining small stocks were being sold competitively. Therefore, transactions were moderate, with high-priced goods, such as Changbang rice, opening at twenty yuan, and lower grades following suit. New early rice dropped by one yuan, with top-grade rice at sixteen yuan, fragrant rice at sixteen yuan fifty cents, and Jiaobaijian, Yangjian, Dujian, and Kejian rice all being dumped by fifty cents to one yuan or more. Top-grade rice is around the thirteen yuan mark. The downward trend here is no less than in North Shanghai, and further declines may be necessary.

Nanjing Autumn Silkworm School Breeding is Better 130

Bake Losses are Only 300 Jin, Only 30% of Expected Silkworm Production.

This Autumn's silkworm crops in the Nanjing markets and countryside were mostly improved breeds (commonly called "School Breeds") made by the Sericulture Department of Jinling University, due to the promotion of trial breeding by silk merchants. The silkworm crop initially was very good, but sudden changes in weather, cold rain, and continuous heavy rains during the hibernation period caused the silkworms to get sick and the harvest was extremely poor, with only 30% of the expected crop. The silkworm quality was best with the School Breeds, with bake losses of only 300 Jin.

Rice Market 142

South Shanghai

Recently, the South Shanghai rice market has seen a surge in arrivals, with about 300 boats accumulating in the Huangpu River, estimated to hold about 27,000 dan of new early rice, white rice, and various kinds of late rice. Therefore, urban and rural trading has been extremely sluggish. Prices of new early rice and fragrant rice have fallen by one yuan, while Jiaobaijian and Dujian rice have fallen by 50 cents. Ocean Point, new Kejian is also weaker and has fallen by two-tenths or more.

Zhabei 143

For days boats have been accumulating, and rice shops watch small and are afraid to bring in too much, thus the sellers are stuck. Yesterday also sixty-seventy boats arrived and eastern and western new rice prices fell by a sharp one to two yuan so sales were stagnant. Kejian, Jiaobaijian, and Dujian prices fell by six to seven jiao, and the remainder all decreased by three to four jiao.

Departing Tomorrow Morning on the Fengtian Maru

Xiong Shihui Replied to Zhang Xueliang via Telegram 194

Stating That One Word Can Revive a Nation, and All Sides Rely On You

Xiong Shihui, Commander of the Songhu Garrison, telegraphed a reply to Zhang Xueliang yesterday, stating:

Extremely Urgent. Commander Zhang, Vice Commander of Shenyang, greetings. I have received your compassionate telegram. Your concern for the country and sympathy for the people are deeply felt. Since the rebellious forces started the unrest several months ago, the communist bandits have seized the opportunity internally, and Soviet Russia is watching for a chance to stir up trouble externally. The fathers and elders in the war zone of Hebei and Henan are suffering as refugees, and the people in the disaster-stricken areas of Shaanxi are burdened by excessive conscription. Yet they still refuse to lay down their arms and insist on their evil ways, hoping to cause more disasters and lead to great upheaval. If we look at the extent of the disaster, it will not only lead to the downfall of the nation and the extinction of the people. Anyone with blood and spirit should feel guilty. Moreover, in your lofty wisdom and profound insight, you have already expressed your grief. The National Government's clear order on the 23rd and the Commander-in-Chief's telegram fully demonstrate their sympathy for the people and their desire for peace. They praised your virtue and granted your request to devote yourself to the party and the country, and to promote peace. One word from you can revive the nation, and all sides rely on you. I hope you will expand your great ambitions and carry out your original intention, basing yourself on the central government's fair approach and striving to push Yan and Feng to step down, so as to secure the country on a firm foundation and consolidate the foundation of unity. This would be a great blessing for the nation. Xiong Shihui bowed with respect.

The Local Rice Market Plummets 195

The Panic Period Has Passed

Processing and Sorting Are Underway

Since the Shanghai rice market began to implement public measures, evaluations, and supervised distribution by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau in June, the rice market has gradually stabilized. Recently, new rice from various regions has flooded in, and the rice-producing areas of Jiangsu Province are also expected to have good harvests, leading to a further decline in prices. When the Dongxin Japonica rice first appeared, it was priced at 21 yuan, and the Xixin Japonica rice also reached 20.5 yuan. Because the supply of old Japonica rice was not connected to the arrival of new rice, and the new rice had not yet reached its peak, it was necessary to appropriately relax restrictions. Recently, the daily arrival of rice has been over 20,000 shi (bushels), and broken rice has almost disappeared. The current price of new top-grade Japonica rice is 15.8 to 17 yuan, which is four yuan less than five days ago. The price of Ke Xian rice is 11 to 11.8 yuan, which is 3.5 yuan less than five days ago. It is also heard that a large amount of rice is on its way, and the market price is expected to fall further. It is reported that the Bureau has not yet revoked the evaluation order for the sake of caution, but it is expected to do so soon. The Bureau is also in the process of sorting and editing the complex circumstances of this year's rice shortage, which will serve as a valuable reference. It is said that it will be published as soon as it is completed.

Hu Ruoyu Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 196

Went to Nanjing with Li Shizeng Last Night

To Attend the Funeral of Director Tan, but Did Not Visit Chiang

Hu Ruoyu, the mayor of Qingdao, arrived in Shanghai at 3:00 PM yesterday on the Fengtian Maru from Qingdao. Li Shizeng and representatives from Finance Minister Song Ziwen, among others, welcomed him at the pier. He then went with Li to Li's private residence on Foch Road to rest. At 11:00 PM last night, Hu and Li took the night train to Nanjing. He will return to Qingdao after a short stay. This trip is purely a personal matter and does not represent Director Zhang, so he will not visit General Chiang at the front line. The rumor that Zhang Xueming is the commander of the Qingdao garrison is absolutely untrue, because a garrison commander must have troops stationed there, and Zhang has no troops stationed in Qingdao, so this rumor is unfounded. As for the facilities of Qingdao's municipal administration, there are no new plans for the time being.

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Orders the Expedited Creation of Household Registers 198

For the Purpose of Dividing Municipal Districts

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau received instructions from the Municipal Government yesterday, stating:

In order to comply with the order of the Executive Yuan to divide the municipal districts of this city, the committee has been organized and decided to conduct a survey and create registers in accordance with the original municipal districts. However, in the four districts of Hunan, Zhabei, Yinxiang, and Yangjing, where municipal committees have not been established, the Public Security Bureau should be responsible for creating household registers in preparation for the division and for formulating a register format to be uniformly created and submitted for review by October 4th. The matter of creating registers is complicated and the deadline is pressing. The Bureau hereby orders you, the station chiefs, to immediately send the household registration patrol officers to the Bureau to receive the registers and await instructions on the household registration procedures. At the same time, the station chiefs should select two clerical police officers in addition to the existing household registration officers and assistants to help with the creation of the registers. They must be completed and submitted to the Bureau by October 2nd, without delay, so as not to hinder the public interest. This order is urgent.

The Issue of Water Rate Increases 201

A Compilation of Correspondence

The following is a compilation of correspondence between the Chinese Ratepayers Association, the Real Estate Association, and the Water Company regarding the issue of water rate increases in the International Settlement:

Letter from the Ratepayers Association to the Public Works Department:

Sir, Regarding the water rate increase, our Association sent a letter on September 16th detailing two major reasons. We believe that you have already considered them. As for your department's reply of September 15th to our Association's first response, when compared with the two letters mentioned in our Association's second letter, the reasons for the rate increase are still difficult to establish. Your department should pay attention to this. Now, the Shanghai Water Company, perhaps at the suggestion of your department, has sent a letter to our Association and the Shanghai Real Estate Association requesting them to send representatives to audit the accounts. From a legal point of view, our Association believes that the water rate increase should be discussed after the audit results are reported. We hereby send this letter for your attention and to inform the Shanghai Water Company.

Letter from the Ratepayers Association to the Company:

Sir, We have received your letter of September 18th requesting our Association to send representatives to audit the accounts. We have learned that your company is a public utility and has requested relevant organizations to audit the accounts. This open attitude is a proper approach. Our Association is a representative organization of all residents in the Settlement, and we have an unshirkable duty to fulfill this responsibility. We hereby appoint Mr. Yu Xiji, a certified accountant and member of our Association, Mr. Pan Xulun, a certified accountant, and Mr. He Dekui, a Master of Commerce, as representatives to conduct the audit. We hereby send this letter for your attention. Furthermore, our Association believes that the issue of water rates should be discussed after the audit results are known. We hereby state this together.

Letter from the Company to the Real Estate Association:

The Shanghai Water Company to the Shanghai Real Estate Association, greetings: We have received your letter of the 23rd requesting the annual report and accounts of our company. We now enclose the business report for the past three years for your review. Our directors believe that the basis for this surcharge is the budget for the coming year. We previously requested your Association to select representatives to review this budget. The past accounts are not related to the current issue. Today's newspapers reported that the Chinese Ratepayers Association has selected three audit representatives. Our directors respectfully request your Association to select specialists to conduct the audit at the same time.

Reply from the Real Estate Association to the Company:

The Shanghai Real Estate Association replied to the Shanghai Water Company yesterday, stating: We have received your letter today enclosing the business report for the past three years. We are aware that your company's attitude is upright and in line with the behavior of a monopolistic public utility. However, your company said that the invited reviewers are only to review the budget based on future revenue and expenditure, and that the past business conditions are not within the scope of review. This is not the same from our Association's point of view. We believe that the future budget must be based on the past. Moreover, since this is the first time to review this economic situation, it is necessary to know its past history in order to be effective. Therefore, we still request your company to send the report of the business operations since its establishment to the Association for reference. As for sending representatives to conduct the audit, our Association believes that it is our natural and unshirkable duty. However, the Chinese Ratepayers Association is the general representative organization of all residents in the Settlement, and our Association has absolute respect for its words and deeds. For the sake of unity, we will not send representatives to conduct the audit this time. We will ask the audit representatives of the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association to do so. In theory, our Association believes that the issue of whether or not to increase the water rate should be discussed after the audit results are known. We have sent this letter for your reference.

Letter from the Real Estate Association to the Ratepayers Association:

The Shanghai Real Estate Association sent a letter to the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association yesterday, stating: Regarding the Shanghai Water Company's request to send representatives to audit the accounts, our Association sent a letter to the company requesting the annual business report since its establishment. Later, we received only one copy of the company's report for the past three years. They also requested that the invited reviewers only review the outline based on future revenue and expenditure, and that the past business conditions were not within the scope of review. How can the company's attitude be known? Therefore, we again sent a letter to the company requesting the business report for reference. As for sending representatives to conduct the audit, although the company has repeatedly urged us to do so, our Association confirms that your Association is the general representative organization of all residents in the Settlement, and we have absolute respect for your Association's words and deeds. For the sake of unity, our Association will not send representatives. We respectfully ask Mr. Yu Xiji, Mr. He Dekui, and Mr. Pan Xulun to take the lead. In addition to informing the Shanghai Water Company for reference, we have also sent this letter for your reference and to extend our regards to the three representatives, Yu, He, and Pan.

Special Transportation Contract Negotiations: China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Customs Brokers Association Reach Understanding 203

Results of Discussions Between Customs Broker Representatives and the Company

After the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (招商局) concluded special transportation contracts with Maoxin (茂新), Fuxin (福新), Shenxin (申新), and other factories in June of this year for flour and cotton yarn, the Customs Brokers Association (報關行同業) sent representatives to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to question whether this would hinder the business of customs brokers. Although the company explained, it did not gain their understanding. Recently, the Customs Brokers Association again sent a letter to the company requesting the maintenance of the rights of the industry and dispatched representatives You Senting (尤森庭) and Shi Zhikun (石芝坤) to the company for discussions. The company has made a sincere statement, and it is hoped that misunderstandings can be resolved. The details of this matter are recorded below:

Content of the Reply: Upon investigation, the practice of shipping companies directly entering into transportation contracts with customers is not new, nor did it originate with our company. For example, Qixin (啓新) Cement Factory, Jiuda (久大), Yijing (益精) Salt Factories in Tianjin, and companies such as the Asiatic Petroleum Company, Standard Oil Company of New York, British-American Tobacco Company in Shanghai, British Soap Company, Tongyutai (通豫泰) and Fuliang (福良) Companies in Jiujiang, and the Ningbo Cotton Industry Association have all entered into transportation contracts with shipping companies for many years. Furthermore, Maoxin, Fuxin, Shenxin, and other factories have also directly contracted with Taikoo (太古) (it is heard that Taikoo already handles the transport of their flour from Shanghai to Hong Kong and Guangdong). All the above-mentioned cases occurred before our company entered into contracts, and we have not heard your association express opposition. There may be some misunderstandings, and we hope for your understanding and consideration.

Representatives’ Discussions: You Senting, chairman of the customs brokers associations in various treaty ports, and Shi Zhikun, chairman of the customs brokers associations in the north and south of the city, visited the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company General Bureau yesterday at 3 PM to inquire about the contents of the contract. Shen Zhongyi (沈仲毅), head of the Business Section, met them, explained everything, and stated that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company entered into transportation contracts with various commercial firms to increase business. All companies have precedents, but the water transport rates set this time are not lower than market prices, so there is no hindrance to the business of customs brokers. The shipping company and the customs brokers association are interdependent, and there is no reason to abandon them. It can be guaranteed that the freight of each customs broker will be loaded first, etc. The two representatives expressed satisfaction and agreed to explain to all their colleagues.

News of the End of the War and the Progress of the Zhong-Longhai Joint Transportation 205

Ministry of Communications Orders Investigation into the Zhen Da Wharf Construction Case

Since the opening of Haizhou (海州) as a seaport, most of the goods from Longhai (隴海), Pingpu (平浦), and Pinghan (平漢) areas that used to be transported to Shanghai were loaded onto Yangtze River boats. Eight or nine out of ten were transferred from Xuzhou (徐州) to Pukou (浦口) and then loaded onto Yangtze River boats to Shanghai. The procedures were complicated, the transport was time-consuming, and the water transport rates were very high. After the waterway directly connecting Haizhou to Shanghai was opened, Longhai goods could be directly loaded onto ships in Haizhou. Therefore, the tobacco from Lanzhou (蘭州), Gansu (甘肅), which used to come to Shanghai by Yangtze River boats, is now transported from Haizhou to Shanghai. In recent years, due to the war, the transportation of goods from Longhai was blocked, and the shipping industry in Haizhou was severely affected. Now that the war is about to end, it is hoped that commercial transportation in Longhai can be restored. The recent situation of Haizhou shipping is recorded below: Currently operating in Haizhou: After the opening of Haizhou to navigation, the first company to start operations was the Japanese-owned International Steamship Company (國際從汽社), which sent two ships to run between Shanghai and Haizhou. There were even more Japanese ships traveling from Qingdao to Haizhou. Last year, after the Ministry of Foreign Affairs strongly argued with the Japanese side that Haizhou was an inland area and not a treaty port, foreign ships could not navigate there, and the Japanese ships between Shanghai and Haizhou stopped. There are still three Japanese ships operating from Qingdao. There are more than a dozen Chinese merchant ships traveling to Haizhou from Shanghai, mostly transporting salt from Lianghuai (兩淮) to the Yangtze River. Because the salt from Huai does not need to be weighed when transported to Shanghai, the maximum number of carriers is formal liners. Initially, there was only one ship, "Tonghua (同華)," from China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. This year, the Da Zhen Company (大振公司) was established and specially opened two regular Shanghai-Haizhou ships.

Longhai Joint Transportation to be Established: The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's opening of the Haizhou route was a plan for the creation of Longhai joint transportation. The plan was formulated, but the war broke out, and the Longhai line became a war zone, so it could not be realized. Now that the military conflict is about to end, the Northwest Army (西北軍) has retreated, and the Longhai line can be restored. A large amount of materials blocked in Shanghai will also be transported there. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's joint transportation plan will also be implemented. Taking advantage of the fact that the Longhai line's military transport is not yet complete, the "Tonghua" ship will temporarily stop running two or three shifts to Haizhou and transport grain to North China. Once the road is open to traffic, it will be ordered to resume sailing. On the other hand, preparations are underway for the necessary procedures for joint transportation.

Recent Ship Accidents: The waters around Dapu (大浦) are not very wide, and the currents are very turbulent, making navigation extremely difficult. There is still a risk of accidents. Last year, the "Hualun (華倫)" was stranded and damaged, and last time the "Tonghua" ran aground. Recently, from August to the present, six salt-carrying ships have run aground there. Initially, the "Yongping (泳平)" and "Yongping (永平)" collided with each other at Dapukou (大浦口), suffering heavy damage. Then, the "Yingfa (英發)" ran aground outside the port and sank, resulting in huge losses. Currently, various shipping merchants have submitted a memorial to the Ministry of Communications requesting dredging of the river, removal of shallow reefs and sandbars to facilitate navigation. The Ministry of Communications has consulted the Jiangsu Provincial Government for thorough investigation to facilitate construction.

Negotiations on Da Zhen Wharf Construction: Da Zhen Company specially purchased land in Dapu, Haizhou, to build a wharf. The Shanghai Merchant Ship Captains Association (本埠商船駕駛總會) presented a memorial to the Ministry of Communications to stop it, stating that Da Zhen is building a wharf outside Yuxingyong Wharf (裕興永碼頭) at the northern end of the port. The water surface here is less than 100 feet wide, which is the narrowest part of the waterway and has the fastest current. The riverbank on the opposite side is curved and has many curves. In addition, the wharf occupies the middle of the channel, causing congestion, and the two banks are almost connected, leaving no place for ships to avoid danger. When the tide is low, the water surface is even narrower, creating a situation of sealing off the port. There have been six or seven accidents in the past month, and the "Yongping" almost crashed into the wharf upon entering the port. Dapu is a densely populated area of the Longhai, Pingpu, and Pinghan lines. In recent years, the number of passengers and goods has been increasing, and the number of ships entering and leaving the port has been increasing daily. Various companies are competing to purchase land to build wharves. However, the port is an inland port and is not under the jurisdiction of the Customs, and the government has not established a competent authority. Shipping merchants operate freely without any restrictions. Those who can control the overall situation due to the strategic location are considered to have a natural monopoly, regardless of traffic obstruction, public safety, and security (omitted). It is impossible to sit idly by and allow the safety of the majority to be harmed for the sake of one company, etc. It is heard that the Ministry of Communications has ordered Donghai County (東海縣) to investigate this case.

Third National Products Promotion Conference 206

Decision to Hold at the National Products Commercial Center

In addition to the National Products Fashion Exhibition and the Salt Conference held at the Dahua Hotel (大華飯店), the remaining activities of the Third National Products Promotion Conference (第三届國貨運動大會), led by the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau (本市社會局), such as exhibitions, displays, recreational activities, and the opening ceremony, have been decided to be held at the China National Products United Commercial Center (中華國産聯合大商塲) on Nanjing Road. Establishment of the Cotton Textile Exhibition Preparatory Committee 207

Opening Date Changed to November 1st

The preparatory committee for the cotton textile exhibition of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's National Products Exhibition Hall (工商部國貨陳列館) held its inaugural meeting yesterday at the Shanghai-based product collection office in Jiu'anli (久安里). Yang Wenquan (楊聞泉), the director of the hall, chaired the meeting and reported on the purpose of the meeting, stating that the cotton textile exhibition is more important than other exhibitions because cotton textiles are more common among the people and not as expensive as other silk and wool textiles. Then, the following items were discussed and resolved: (1) The opening date, originally set for October 10th, has been postponed to November 1st due to insufficient preparation. (2) The Shanghai National Products Factory Federation (上海國貨工廠聯合會) (address: 713 Jiu'anli) will be used as the product collection office in Shanghai. (3) Transportation will be reduced in fees and exempted from taxes. (4) It is planned to hire directors for the collection of various items. (5) Sales methods and display procedures will be stipulated, and photography, tea, and refreshments will be provided at the end of the meeting.

Chen Yingshi Memorial Tower 209

Completion Ceremony Scheduled for the Shanghai Restoration Day

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works (上第市工務局) recently sent a letter to this newspaper stating that yesterday (25th), various newspapers in Shanghai (note: this newspaper did not publish it) widely reported that the completion ceremony of the Chen Yingshi (陳英士) Memorial Tower in Ximen (西門) would be held on October 10th, which is not true. Since the tower's construction began on May 18th of this year, the anniversary of Mr. Yingshi's martyrdom, it has been four months. Record of the Standing Committee Meeting of the Red Cross Society 211

The 102nd Meeting

The Chinese Red Cross Society held its 102nd Standing Committee meeting on September 22nd. The attending committee members included Jian Lantang, Wang Boqi, Ha Shaofu, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Peiyuan, Tan Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Tan Rongpu, Yao Yuqin, Yuan Zhongwei, Huang Hanzhi, Zhang Tiemin, etc. Chairman Wang Yiting, and Recorder Wei Ruifeng conducted the proceedings according to protocol. The minutes of the previous meeting were read, and without any objections from the members, the Chairman signed them. (1) The Chairman reported that, according to newspaper reports, the Ministry of Interior, acting on the instructions of the Executive Yuan, had interpreted the Chinese Red Cross Society as a local charitable organization, subject to the supervision of the local government in accordance with the regulations for supervising charitable organizations. He had gone to Beijing to visit Tan Yankai, President of the Executive Yuan, Zhang Jiazeng, Vice Minister of the Interior, and Wang Zhengting, Minister of Foreign Affairs, to clarify that the Red Cross Society is an international charitable legal entity, not comparable to local charitable organizations, and is directly under the Central Government, so it should not be subject to the supervision of local governments. President Tan Yankai, Vice Minister Zhang Jiazeng, and Minister Wang Zhengting all agreed to maintain this stance, resulting in a very satisfactory outcome. It was resolved that a detailed report on the history of the Society be submitted to the Chairman of the National Government. He also mentioned that President Tan Yankai was deeply concerned about the dire situation in Hunan due to the disaster and hoped that the Society would provide assistance, requesting a public decision. It was also publicly discussed that, given the severe disaster in Liaoxi Suizhong, an appeal for urgent relief had already been published in the newspaper. Following President Tan Yankai's request, additional fundraising for disaster relief in Hunan should be initiated. (1) Jian Lanting reported that the regulations and by-laws of the Chinese Red Cross Society and its branches, as well as the election law, had been passed through the third reading by the Committee on Revision of the Constitution. The detailed rules of the Executive Committee of the Society had also been drafted by the Committee on Revision of the Constitution and had been passed through the third reading. He requested that the attending committee members review each item today. Wei Ruifeng then read out the regulations of the Chinese Red Cross Society. Wang Xiaolai suggested that Article 57, regarding the awarding of various medals of merit and the accompanying colored ribbons, might be inconsistent with the current system and should be deleted. He requested a public decision. The members agreed without objection. The remaining items were deemed satisfactory and passed. Wei Ruifeng then read out the by-laws of the branches and the election law, which were also deemed appropriate. Wei Ruifeng then read out the detailed rules of the Executive Committee. Lin Kanghou suggested that the compilation of credit reports was within the purview of the Economic Affairs Department, and that Item 6 of Article 17 should be moved to after Item 4 of Article 13, becoming Item 5. The original Item 5 should be changed to Item 6. The members agreed without objection and passed the motion. Jian Lanting suggested that the above-mentioned passed regulations should first be reported to the National Government for review and record. A public decision was made to proceed accordingly. (1) Jian Lanting proposed that Ms. Ketu, Youth Minister of the International Red Cross League, and Mr. Hausi, Youth Minister of the American Red Cross General Branch of the National Society, had visited the Society and stated that the Red Cross Societies of various countries attach great importance to youth members. However, the methods for managing youth members require specialized knowledge, and it would be best to send someone to study at the Youth Department of the American Red Cross. Upon completion of their studies, they could manage this matter. He, along with Chairman Wang, had discussed the matter, and Wang Yaoting, who is proficient in English, could be sent for study, but it would require an expenditure of 500 yuan. He requested a public decision. Lin Kanghou suggested that if he can serve the Red Cross and seek benefits for the Red Cross after completing his studies, why skimp on the expense of 500 yuan? A public decision was made to proceed accordingly. (1) It was also proposed that although the Epidemic Hospital had been closed on the 20th of this month, cases of Vibrio cholerae and autumn dysentery have recently broken out. The Bureau of Health has sent a letter requesting that the hospital continue to operate. It is now proposed to retain a small number of staff for diagnosis and treatment of epidemics. He requested a public decision. A public decision was made to proceed accordingly. (1) It was also proposed that the members of the Committee on Revision of the Constitution had worked diligently in revising the constitution this time and had made outstanding contributions. How should they be rewarded? He requested a public decision. A public decision was made to wait until all revisions of the constitution are completed before submitting them to the Society for review. (1) It was also proposed that the family members of the director of the Beishi Hospital are still residing in the hospital and have not yet moved out. How should this be resolved? A public decision was made that Chairman Wang should send a letter urging them to move out as soon as possible. (1) Wang Peiyuan proposed that the Society's regulations stipulate that a general meeting for soliciting members should be held every year in October. The time is approaching, and the disasters in Hunan and Liaoxi are extremely severe. The Society urgently needs to solicit donations for disaster relief. Appointing staff to handle the matter separately and widely publicizing it is necessary to expand membership and raise significant funds. He requested a public decision. A public decision was made to proceed accordingly. (1) It was proposed that the Relief and Fundraising Department had promised to allocate 1,000 yuan to the Kunming branch for gunpowder disaster relief. However, because the branch had not submitted a detailed report of income and expenditure, the payment was delayed. After the Relief and Fundraising Department was closed, this amount was not allocated. Now that the disaster relief funds have been almost completely allocated, there are no funds to allocate again. The branch has repeatedly sent letters requesting payment. How should this be resolved? A public decision was made that, since the Relief and Fundraising Department has been abolished, it would not be appropriate to give the funds again, and a letter should be sent to the branch explaining the situation. (1) It was proposed that a pre-donation from a household donated a single paper share certificate of Taichang Electric Light shares with a face value of 1,000 yuan to the Society. It is now worth one-quarter of its value. Fifty shares of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway stock are worth 5 yuan per share, and they can now be exchanged for public bonds, each worth 6 jiao. If a way to convert them into cash is not found soon, they may become worthless paper in the future. He requested a public decision. A public decision was made to convert them into cash separately. (1) It was proposed that Huang Zijing, the director of the Beishi Hospital, had reported in a letter that a student, Chen Jingsheng, had served in the hospital for more than six years. He was usually cautious in his work but unfortunately died of illness on the morning of the 4th of this month. His monthly salary of 8 yuan during his service at the hospital was extremely meager, so his family is destitute and he left behind a wife who is truly pitiful. He requested a pension. A public decision was made to grant a pension of 100 yuan. (1) It was proposed that the Haozhou branch had requested a subsidy due to the severity of the disaster and had already given membership badges to 80 regular members. He requested recognition of the case. A public decision was made to approve the recognition. (1) It was proposed that the Linru Dazhuangzhen, Shantou, Funing, Shimen, Jiaxian, Huangxian, Xiajin, and Zouping branches had requested subsidies for badges or incentives. Cao Qiweng of Yuting had lost his meritorious service badge. He requested that it be reissued. He had raised more than 1,000 yuan for disaster relief and introduced many members. It is not easy to introduce members to establish a branch. Can the foundation membership fee be paid at half price? He requested a public decision and asked that investigators be appointed to review the case one by one. Ha Shaofu and Yao Yuqin were publicly nominated as investigators. The meeting adjourned at more than 7 o'clock.

Record of the Standing Committee Meeting of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce 212

The 13th Meeting

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce held its 13th Standing Committee meeting yesterday afternoon. The attending committee members included Wang Xiaolai, Ye Huijun, Xu Jikui, Fang Jiaobo, etc. The following resolutions were passed: (1) Discussion of the proposal by Standing Committee Member Wang Yansong regarding the method of urging seven or more stores in the same industry to form an industry association. The decision was made to hand it over to the Commerce Section. (2) Discussion of the request by the World Red Swastika Society for donations on its behalf. The decision was made to reply that the local disaster relief and consolation association had already allocated funds to the Disaster Relief Committee for war zone disaster relief. (3) Discussion of the report submitted by Ye Xiaoshan, the officer of the Exhibition Hall, regarding the accounts receivable and payable and the inventory list of the Sales Department. The decision was made to hand it over to the Finance Section for thorough investigation and strict recovery. (4) Discussion of the Commerce Section's report on investigating the name of the Salt Industry Corporation and the salt merchants' overdue debts lawsuit. The decision was made to hand it over to the Commerce Section for reinvestigation. (5) Discussion of the Commerce Section's reply to Qishi's request to establish a branch office. The decision was made to seek instructions from the Social Affairs Bureau. (6) Discussion of the Commerce Section's investigation into the process of persuading Gonghe Lai Paint Shop to join the industry association. The decision was made to recommend Committee Member Fang Jiaobo to persuade them further. (7) Discussion of the method for settling the outstanding printing fees of the former Commercial Monthly. The decision was made to repay them in installments. (8) Discussion of the guarantee letter for the association staff. The decision was made to pass it. (9) Discussion of the guarantee letter for the association workers. The decision was made to pass it.

A passenger ship encounters danger mid-route 213

Fortunately, everyone is safe

The Taikoo Company's Poyang Wheel was shot at by bandits on both sides of the shore with guns and cannons in places such as Xinhekou and Haoxue, Liushuigou in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. The naval soldiers stationed on the Poyang Wheel also fired machine guns, killing two bandits in Xinhekou. Additionally, when the Datong Wheel sailed upstream with the Poyang Wheel, it was fired upon by bandits more than ten times in Xinhekou, but none of the shots hit. The British soldiers on the Datong Wheel returned fire with more than 370 machine-gun rounds. According to reports, more than thirteen or fourteen bandits on the shore were killed. The ships will not be going to the upper reaches of the Yangtze again after this trip. According to the Zi Lin News, the Taikoo's Fengtian Wheel sailed from Shanghai to the north a few days ago. After arriving in Yantai, a fire suddenly broke out in one of the cargo holds, and the goods loaded inside were slightly damaged. However, the ship's hull was undamaged. The cause of the fire is unknown.

News from Various Labor Unions 214

The Xiang Sheng Iron Factory Workers' Union held its third representative assembly the day before yesterday. Chairman Lu Lianqing gave his report. Discussions were held on (1) Whether the union should hold a large-scale celebration for the National Day commemoration. The decision was made to hold a large-scale celebration. (2) The economic measures for preparing the National Day commemoration program should be planned concretely first, and a preparatory committee should be appointed. The decision was made that each representative would be responsible for one yuan. (3) Whether the factory should be notified about holding a National Day commemoration event and whether it should participate in advertising. If it does participate, should there be a subsidy from the factory? A public decision was requested. The decision was made to proceed accordingly. (4) Please appoint a preparatory committee to prepare all matters for the National Day commemoration event. The decision was made to publicly nominate Sun Yushou, Shen Ziting, Zhang Mingbao, Zhu Laifa, Fan Fusheng, Yang A'er, Zhang Xinfu, Shi Yueheng, Wang Guozhen, and nine others as members of the preparatory committee. (5) It was decided to convene the first meeting of the National Day Commemoration Preparatory Committee tomorrow at 5:00 PM to assign duties. The decision was made to pass the motion. (6) Shang Dejun, a representative of the Inspection Department, raised the issue that the department was ordered by the foreman not to open the gates before the workers were dismissed, fearing that workers might misunderstand. He requested that the factory be reasoned with. A public decision was requested. The decision was made to negotiate with the factory to open the gates when the workers are dismissed. (7) Sun Yushou of the Plier Bed Department raised the issue that more than 70 workers in the department were previously expelled from membership for failing to comply with the union's orders. Now, the 70 workers in the department are quite aware of their mistakes and have been re-registered by the union this term. They will absolutely abide by the union's regulations in the future. Should the public be notified? A discussion was requested. The decision was made to publish it in this month's journal.

The Ship Woodworkers' Union held its 5th joint executive and supervisory committee meeting yesterday. Chairman Ye Xianggao made the following resolutions: (1) Pan Gaoxiu, the foreman of He Xing Factory, denied that the wage increase caused a strike and declared that he would not resume work until uniform wages were achieved, and issued a statement requesting evaluation from all sectors. (2) The decision was made to endorse the pursuit of the He Xing Factory strike case, which has been submitted to higher-level authorities, and to immediately send personnel to negotiate to prevent the strike from expanding. (3) Confidential. (4) The attendance of observers at the dismissal meeting will still be handled according to the previous case. (5) Committee Member Luo Buhua returned to Guangdong due to personal reasons and was temporarily replaced by Lin Jingchu. (6) Comrade Chen Yaoshen reported that the audit of the accounts of the first session was accurate and that the rest was slightly omitted.
